###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Symbols for Logical Operators

_(reply depth: 5)_

- **From:** robert@wagner.net (Robert Wagner)
- **Date:** 2003-06-04T23:51:59+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3ede6c0d.522812173@news.optonline.net>`
- **References:** `<bbgn0a$11u7$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <3edc0d2e.367429814@news.optonline.net> <01c329f9$9f7a6520$64ccf943@chottel> <bbiqfd$2j0g$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <bbktdg$lll$1@slb9.atl.mindspring.net>`

```
Because you and Chuck Stevens are opposed, my suggestion has no hope of being
seriously considered much less approved. I will retract (cancel, delete) it
within a day or two. 

What J4 taketh away, Micro Focus giveth. The program below compiles and executes
correctly. Finally! I can write logic statements with consistent notation, even
though J4 doesn't want me to.

Lessons learned. This episode has weakened my support for the Standards process
and nudged me toward PECD's stance of 'with friends like these, COBOL doesn't
need enemies.'  I used to say stick with the Standard unless there's significant
benefit from departing. Henceforth I'll depart when there is ANY benefit. The
notion that we'll be required to change platforms tomorrow is illusory FUD. 99%
of COBOL will never be ported to another platform. If it is, a competent text
editor could do these particular transformations to dozens of programs in less
than a minute of typing.

The real issue is controlling vs. permissive style. Some people want to be
controlled (e.g. DD), some want to fly free.  J4 is controlling; Micro Focus and
my personal style are permissive. J4 doesn't address my (our) needs, so we'll
look elsewhere. History will report whether minions or iconoclasts prevailed. 

Recommended Reading for more on evolution vs. revolution: "Notes on the
Synthesis of Form", Christopher Alexander, Harvard Press. On the surface it's
about architecture but its lessons apply to all system development. It supports
conservative evolutionary growth with more rationale and intelligence than most
on that side of the issue. 

Robert

      $SET SOURCEFORMAT"FREE"
 identification division.
 program-id. test32.
*  author. Robert Wagner.
*   Testing symbolic logical operators.
*
*   ADDSYN accepts only COBOL characters.
*   REPLACE takes any "text word" in Micro Focus mode; rejects
*   non-COBOL characters in Standard mode.
*   For some idiosynchratic reason, != works but !< does not.
*   The last two replacements fix that problem.
*
*   copy 'symbols'.
      REPLACE ==!==by==NOT ==
              ==^==by==AND ==
              ==|==by==OR ==
              ==!<==by==>= ==
              ==!>==by==<= ==.

 procedure division.

    if 1=0 | 1 !< 0 ^ 2 != 0 ^ !(1=0)
        display '1. true'  *> should be true
    else
        display '1. false'
    end-if
 .

```
Just so you (Robert) and any others reading this thread actually CARED about
what was said below:

1) Chuck *does* currently represent a member organization at J4.  Therefore,
he has an "official" voice at J4 (and depending upon other factors may be
part of the US delegation to WG4).  I am *not* a member of J4 (anymore).
Therefore, I have no more "say" than anyone else.

2) If there were an "enhancement" that actually DID receive overwhelming
support within comp.lang.cobol, it would be my guess that it also MIGHT get
a good reception at J4/WG4.  However, making a proposal here and hearing
"mostly silence" - and a few "wouldn't objects" is NOT the same as
overwhelming support.

3) I still believe that ALL proposals sent to J4 *do* get a "serious
consideration" regardless of what individuals (in or out of that committee)
feel about it.  See Chuck's several notes on how *he* would oppose enhancing
"combined abbreviated relation conditions" *BUT* he could not/would not
speak for what the COMMITTEE would do with such.

   ***

If anyone in this group has ideas for future enhancements that they want to
submit to J4, I think that Robert's experience DOES teach a lesson.  It
really is a good idea to present your "actual" proposal to the full CLC and
request (and listen to) what others say about it.  If the feeling is "luke
warm" or many people don't CARE about it, the chances are that it MAY well
get the same reception at J4.  SILENCE is reply is NOT a positive response!
```

There was overwhelming support for symbolic relational operators. I extrapolated
that to logical operators, which were discussed only tangentally. For instance,
at least twice I was asked 'Suppose there were symbols for logical operators.
Would you then be opposed to symbolic relational operators?'. I answered "No. If
the notation was complete, I'd use symbols for everything." That started my
mental gears turning and prompted the request. 

>If anyone in this group has ideas for future enhancements that they want to
>submit to J4, I think that Robert's experience DOES teach a lesson.  It
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>get the same reception at J4.  SILENCE is reply is NOT a positive response!

Since the request was coming from me, group review was not *required*. Under
ordinary conditions, I would have posted it here as a matter of courtesy. I
didn't in this case because I knew what would have happened .. and subsequently
did happen. Whatever position I supported, the vocal members of the group would
oppose. 

When I argued for words, they wanted symbols. After I switched sides, I was
somehow STILL wrong. The debate wasn't about ideas, it was about politics. It
was about getting even for perceived insults in the past on other issues. Thus
the proposal would not have received a fair review here. People trying to be
objective, as you have been, would have been shouted down.

jallan:
I find the c notation clearest: a = b || !(a >= c) || a >= d

The structure of the statement is so much better indicated at a
glance.

http://groups.google.com/groups?q=greater+cobol+jallan&hl=en&lr=lang_en&ie=UTF-8&oe=UTF-8&newwindow=1&safe=off&selm=299f1138.0305250755.30e384d1%40posting.google.com&rnum=2

Tukla Ratte:
But Robert must sit and stare at a "<" for a few seconds to determine
if it means "is less than" or "is greater than".  Because he has
difficulties with something that 99.99% of other programmers handle
reflexively, it is a Bad Thing.

This has been a great thread.  I've always wondered who used those
bulky, spelled-out conditionals.  Now I know.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Richard:
Actually I find that keeping my style consistent with other languages
helps, not only when I switch languages, but also to others who may
read my code and may have been taught others.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Chuck Stevens:
Now, the other side of that same point:  The framers of the latest standard
for COBOL have worked diligently to rectify COBOL's historical bias toward
American usage.  For those not literate in English, "IF A >= B" is more
legible than "IF A IS GREATER THAN OR EQUAL TO B".
--------------------------------------------------------------

robert@wagner.net (Robert Wagner) wrote 

> Read again. I said _relational_ operators. There were more than a hundred ..
> excuse me, make that >100 .. postings supporting > over GREATER THAN.

There were many, many postings supporting 'what I am used to'.  What
they were used to was '>' '<' '=' and also AND, OR, NOT.

These many, many, postings did not like the words 'GREATER THAN' for
exactly the reason that they were unfamiliar with seeing it and thus
it took more time to recognise what it was doing than the use of the
symbols they were familiar with. There was also the issue of having to
scan such things as 'greater than or equal to' compared to a much
shorter '>='.

Your symbols take _longer_ to understand because it is necessary to
get used to them, and they are insignificantly shorter than what they
replace.

You have incompetently extrapolated their 'we like what was are used
to' into your: 'therefore you like what you are not used to'.

As I said, using your logic I may take your preference for a gourmet
mushroom dish to also mean you would like a Fillet Mignon.

But you _also_ fraudulently (or perhaps ignorantly) claimed that
programmers of other languages would prefer something that they were
not used to, or used for different purposes, rather than using what
they already did in their languages (as indicated previously).

Nobody cares whether you use words, symbols or Low German via a
pre-processor, just as long as you don't do it in our site. What we do
care about (as is obvious) is the lies and misrepresentations that you
make.
```

program and also what I will use on READ NOT AT END.

Or were you also going to propose changes there.
 
> That's a valid point. I'll change the suggestion to use C symbols, although
> I'm not crazy about stuttering diagraphs.

Then don't propose them.  What point are you trying to make ?  Change
for change sake ? Argument for argument sake ?

You can use whatever you want with REPLACE or preprocessor, so can
anyone else.

robert@wagner.net (Robert Wagner) wrote 

> >Would they ?  Why would C/Java programmers be writing Cobol ?
> 
> I recently worked in two places full of C programmers who occasionally
> maintained legacy Cobol. 

And where in 'legacy code' would they find symbols for and/or/not ? 
Did you expect that overnight the code would be revised automatically
by the acceptance of your proposal ? So how would your proposal help
them in that way ? (clue: it wouldn't).

Given that it is 'legacy code' that 'legacy Cobol programmers' (ie
non-C/Java) may be expected to also work on, how would allowing C/Java
programmers write symbols that these legacy coders were unfamiliar
with help reliability and maintainability of the code ? (clue: it
wouldn't).

Given that legacy code may be kept alive with legacy compilers, how is
this relevant at all. (clue: it isn't).

You often seem to make up an argument by writing down the first thing
that pops into your head with no real thought about whether it is at
all sensible. ie superficial and arbitrary springs to mind to describe
these. There is no substance to your argument, especially this one.

> I resubmitted the Enhancement Request specifying C/Java symbols as my first
> choice, and deleting any reference to CLC. 

So, you do agree that your whole proposal was worth junking
completely.

> >How does using something else that no Cobol programmer has used, nor
> >Perl, Python, SQL, VB, etc rate on 'familiarity' ?
> 
> They already have familiar words and symbols (except <>). The request will
> accomodate C/Java writers.

So, after a C/Java programmer has worked on the code it won't matter
that it will not longer be familiar to Cobol/Python/SQL/VB/Perl/etc
writer ?

What will happen when a C/Jave programmer writes '! AT EBD' ?  does
your proposal cover this ?  Is this a sensible use of a symbol ?

To pander to C/Java have you also proposed EOF instead of AT END so
that they can write:

      READ file EOF action1 !EOF action2 END-READ

What if they write embedded SQL with WHERE .. || .. ?  

Have you also proposed these changes to ANSI SQL so that this can be
consitent with C/Java and with your new proposal ?

You are you expecting C/Java programmers to cope with and/or/not for
existing Cobol code and for embedded SQL and (probably) for NOT AT
END. They have to know _existing_ Cobol, so what _gain_ do they have ?

You are expecting C/Java programmers to polute Cobol with !/||/&& so
that it makes it _less_ understandable to Cobol/Python/SQL/Perl/VB etc
programmers.  So what is the _gain_ ?

Now there _may_ be a point if there was a demand for C/Java
programmers to write new modern programs in Cobol (_not_ maintaining
existing ones) so that they could write them as if they were C
programs. In this way C/Java programmers would not have to learn
and/or/not.  But this is trivial compared to the rest of the language.
 So where is the gain ?

In any case modern Cobol programs may be SQL in which case they
_would_ have to learrn and/or/not anyway.

But I see no demand for this from anyone:

  - not from C/Java needing to maintain existing code (which has
and/or/not),
  - not from _owners_ of legacy code (who would certainly not want it
made
      unmaintainable for legacy Cobol programmers).
  - not from C/Java programmers wanting to write new Cobol (they
don't).
  - not from existing Cobol programmers - certainly not ones here
(perhaps one).
  - not from 'purists' seeking some crap about 'symmetry'.

So far your proposal seems to make code _less_ maintainable without
any apparent gain.

So why are you making this proposal - make a _real_ justification.
```

They can do that right now, and then after they have modified it they
can run it again and put the && back to AND before the compile.  In
fact you could have been doing this for years if it was of any use to
anyone at all.

How hard is this ?  You don't need to whine about this, just do it if
you want it.

Of course, and you may not know this, changing AND into && does not
make Cobol be the same as C.  Having it _almost_ look the same is
likely to be less productive than having it be Cobol.  C programmers
use C idioms, these can't be done in Cobol. Making it look _almost_
right will make for more errors.

If you want to discuss the _future_ of Cobol then stop trying to make
it into a second class C.

…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> Ad hominem #3. 

You make superficial arguments and I will tell you that is what they
are.

In fact you can't seem to make up your mind as to what you are trying
to achieve.  You want to make legacy code into 2nd class C so it
doesn't need Cobol programmers, then you talk about 'the future' ?

Is the future to be catering for handing all code to C/Java
programmers to look after ?

> >writer ?

Are you implying that Cobol/Python/SQL/VB/Perl/etc programmers are
'dull-witted'?  Is it only C/Java programmers that are not
'dull-witted'?

And why do you imply any association between 'familiarity' and
'dull-witted' ?


> >What will happen when a C/Jave programmer writes '! AT END' ?  does
> >your proposal cover this ?  Is this a sensible use of a symbol ?
> 
> It's a straw man. In forty years, I've never written NOT AT END. 

For a start you wouldn't have been able to for most of that time -
perhaps you didn't know that.  But it is irrelevant that you don't
write modern Cobol, many of us do.

But it is not a straw man argument, but a sustantial one. Your
proposal makes the symbol usage inconsistent as a substitute for NOT. 
In fact your 'never used that' is the real straw man here.
 

> These are Red Herring arguments. I'm unconcerned with SQL standards, just
>  COBOL. Let's try to stay focussed. 

I am focussed.  I see my programs with and/or/not in the embedded SQL
and 'NOT' in other syntax.  On the one hand you want 'the future' yet
you ignore modern Cobol because what you have written is 20 year old

Your plan is to have inconsistent use of and/or/not.

> >You are you expecting C/Java programmers to cope with and/or/not for
> >existing Cobol code and for embedded SQL and (probably) for NOT AT
> >END. They have to know _existing_ Cobol, so what _gain_ do they have ?
> 
> Existing code could easily be translated by a beautifier. 

Then please feel free to do that, and beautify it back as part of the
compile process.  In fact if you want symbols for and/or/not in the
SQL you will need to do that anyway.

You have just argued that your proposal is completely unrequired.
 
> >You are expecting C/Java programmers to polute Cobol with !/||/&& so
> >that it makes it _less_ understandable to Cobol/Python/SQL/Perl/VB etc
> >programmers.  So what is the _gain_ ?
> 
> A common symbology. 

What makes '\/' common to '||'  (or 'or' in the embedded SQL) ?
What makes '^'  common to '&&'  (or 'amd' in embedded SQL) ?
What make '~'   common to '!'   (or 'not' in embedded SQL) ?

(Given that you have proposed several different symbols).

Will you also be proposing changes to Python/Perl/VB/SQL etc so that
theirs can be 'common' too ?
 
> If we don't make the transition, as appears likely, that will never happen.
> C/Java programmers will write new programs in C/Java and dismiss COBOL as a
> dinosaur, as they have been doing for twenty years. 

Excuse me, but did you think that making a change to '^', '|', '!'
will suddenly cause a stampede of C/Java programmers to writing in
Cobol ?

Making Cobol into a 3rd rate semi-copy of C will just make the C/Java
programmers laugh at you harder than they already do.

You need to consider Cobol's strengths and not C's weaknesses.

Cobol's strength is that code written 30 years ago is readily
understood today. You are trying to change that.
 
> I'm unhappy with seeing my favorite language marginalized because its
> standards process has been, and continues to be,  unresponsive. 

And how does throwing more silly proposals at the J4 help ?  You give
them _more_ work to do, slowing down the process, instead of taking up
the offers of being a helper in the process.

Anyway the reason that your programming manager wants to dump all the
Cobol and rewrite in C is less to do with the language than it has to
do with getting rid of a programmer with the social skills of
sandpaper.

> >So why are you making this proposal - make a _real_ justification.
> 
> I have many times. Let's not replow that ground.

No. You haven't.  You have not made one real justification for
replacing and/or/not with symbols.  Not one.

The C/Java thing is entirely spurious, most of the symbols proposed
are not C/Java or mean different things.  In any case C/Java
programmers do not want to write Cobol. Looking after legacy code is
spurious because legacy compilers won't have the change
retrospectively added. Everything that you want to do can be done
without language changes by the very beautifier you would use.  You
haven't shown any _gains_ at all in productivity or maintainability,
in fact quite the reverse.

You haven't even shown that your proposal's claim of 'C/Java would
welcome it' to be anything other than a silly wish.  Why _would_ they
welcome \//\~ or ^|! or some of the other symbols ?  Why even would
they welcome a half-baked change to being almost similar to a sub-set
of what they use ?

As for 'consistency' !hah.  It isn't.

you could use it or not and when).  Others do use it, and C/Java
programmers _may_ want to.

There is more to making a proposal than just tossing together a
handful of random symbols and saying 'I want these'.  You need to show
that there actually is an advantage to them, show that it is not just
you wanting them (and  not just lying about support or welcome), that
it cannot be done another way as easily, _and_ that it doesn't lean to
anomolies or ambiguities.

'I want' bit, and haven't even shown which of the grab bag are useful,
then my question was directed at trying to make you _think_ about the

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Standard and REPLACE (was: J4 (was: Symbols for Logical Operators

- **From:** "William M. Klein" <wmklein@ix.netcom.com>
- **Date:** 2003-06-08T16:55:34-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bc0bcq$ril$1@slb9.atl.mindspring.net>`
- **References:** `<bbgn0a$11u7$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <3ede6c0d.522812173@news.optonline.net> <bbmhd0$fos$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net> <3edf2034.568937758@news.optonline.net> <bbnb5q$ssc$1@panix1.panix.com> <3ee044db.643868827@news.optonline.net> <217e491a.0306061424.36bc2612@posting.google.com> <3ee246ee.125515285@news.optonline.net> <217e491a.0306071654.3f65d82e@posting.google.com> <3ee34654.190906920@news.optonline.net>`

```
"Robert Wagner" <robert@wagner.net> wrote in message
news:3ee34654.190906920@news.optonline.net...
> riplin@Azonic.co.nz (Richard) wrote:
<snip>
>
> >You can use whatever you want with REPLACE or preprocessor, so can
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Let's PRETEND for a moment that one actually wanted to use the NON-COBOL \
(backslash) character with REPLACE to allow "/\" and "\/" as "and" and "or"
respectively.  There *is* a way that this may be done with an '85 Standard
compiler.

Suppose you cant to code (with symbols) the equivalent of:

   If (A = B) and ((C > D) or (E < F))

One may (using '85 Standard rules) code:

 Replace =="/\"== by ==and==
               =="\/"== by ==or==
                   .

 If (A = B) "/\" ((C > D) "\/" (E < F))

The same technique will work with ANY *non* COBOL characters.  I
(personally) don't see any advantage to this (over using the native COBOL
*words*) but if one really WANTS to use symbols rather than words *and* one
wants to remain standard-conforming, this will do it.

For that matter, if one HAS "Unicode" characters available (while editing
COBOL source code) one could even code (and hopefully my newsgroup "poster"
won't distort this):

Replace =="?"== by ==and==
              =="?"== by ==or==
                   .

 If (A = B) "?" ((C > D) "?" (E < F))
```

_(reply depth: 14)_

- **From:** "Chuck Stevens" <charles.stevens@unisys.com>
- **Date:** 2003-06-09T12:31:10-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bc2n9v$1la3$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com>`
- **References:** `<bbgn0a$11u7$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <3ede6c0d.522812173@news.optonline.net> <bbmhd0$fos$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net> <3edf2034.568937758@news.optonline.net> <bbnb5q$ssc$1@panix1.panix.com> <3ee044db.643868827@news.optonline.net> <217e491a.0306061424.36bc2612@posting.google.com> <3ee246ee.125515285@news.optonline.net> <217e491a.0306071654.3f65d82e@posting.google.com> <3ee34654.190906920@news.optonline.net>`

```
"Robert Wagner" <robert@wagner.net> wrote in message
news:3ee34654.190906920@news.optonline.net...

> >You can use whatever you want with REPLACE or preprocessor, so can
> >anyone else.
>
> The standard requires COBOL characters in REPLACE.

Which is precisely why I suggested that you consider adding the characters
to COBOL before using them.  The standard *also* requires COBOL characters
in syntax.  Once they're in the list of characters, there's no *practical*
reason to change the standard to allow the abbreviations, because the
standard would *already* allow you to define the substitutions yourself.

You've been arguing "freedom of choice" at some length.

If the characters ^!| were added to the Basic Special Character list in the
COBOL standard, does not *in addition* specifying these characters *in the
standard* as synonyms for the logical operators AND, NOT and OR
significantly *restrict* the programmer's ability to use them in other
contexts for other purposes?

Presuming the characters are in that list, and have no defined syntactic
function elsewhere, a programmer *could, if he desired* (at least in
theory), code "REPLACE ==^== by ==STRING==, ==|== by ==UNSTRING==, ==!== by
==INSPECT==".

Why do you wish to *prevent* him from doing so, and how is that *enhancing
his* ability to code exactly the way he wants to?

I can see supporting the addition of other characters already specified in
ISO/IEC 646 to the Basic Special Character list of the COBOL standard as
providing the programmer additional *choices*.  But specifying that those
special characters have a specific meaning in COBOL takes those choices away
again.

    -Chuck Stevens



    -Chuck Stevens


If the symbols ^!| are added to the standard Basic Special Character list,
then the
```

majority (not universal) objection to your posts that CLAIM that one of two
styles is "superior" to another.  Yes, the majority (of those who posted)
disagreed with your OPINION that "words were superior to symbols"; yes, the
majority (of those who posted) disagreed with your opinion that "symbols
were superior to words"; yes, the majority (of those who posted) disagreed
that there was a "requirement" to provide a complete set of both symbols and
words - because "symmetry" was superior to how things have been for 40
years, i.e. some operators requiring words, some requiring symbols, and some
allowing both.  Do you see (really understand) how/why these views are NOT
contradictory?

Once you really understand why your views of the SUPERIORITY of one style
over another are so often rejected, it will help (along with getting facts
correct and distinguishing opinion from fact) you to receive better
reception of ideas and opinions (here and at J4).

My point (in my original note) was that getting input from this group may
well be a good (not perfect) indicator of how J4 will receive an enhancement
request.  That is why I suggested that you (or anyone else with enhancement
ideas) DO explicitly post their ideas here and see how they are received.
Then they can make the suggestion to J4 (STILL representing it as a personal
suggestion) but with a better idea of how it might be received.
```

other guy's opinion is 'worse' today, yours will be on the chopping block
tomorrow.' That's a tenet of people knowing their position is weak .. people on
the defensive. 

In programming, unlike athletics, playing defense is a losing tactic. We should
be AHEAD of the competition (C#), not behind and whining about lack of
documentation.

```
Ah, ha ... a few easy "answers"

Re:
  "I thought CLC is, among other things, a debate forum."

NO.  There is nothing to "preclude" this - but I think that if you use
google to search for posts before YOU started posting, there was VERY LITTLE
debate. (Certainly some - but not much.)  This is an "open" forum, so anyone
who wants to, may post whatever they want.  HOWEVER, most of us have (and
continue to) feel that the "best" uses of this forum are:

 - provide information to those with "problems" or "questions"
 - expose new (and old) programmers to information on techniques and
products they may not be familiar with
 - share OPINIONS (possibly with "history") - but not try and argue them

        ***

Re;
 "We should have first debated Symmetry: Worthy Objective or Idealistic
Dream?"

or totally irrelevant and not particularly desirable - much less necessary

        ***

Re:
 "My understanding, correct me if I'm wrong, says the aversion to
better/worse, superior/inferior harkens to the Golden Rule. "

No, the "rule" within CLC is that *if* there are two (or more) "styles" of
programming that provide the same functionality, then without OVERWHELMING
evidence to the contrary, they are BOTH valid - and the chances are that for
those "used to" each, each is equally "maintainable", "user-friendly", etc.
Maters of style are NOT going to get much (if any) support for being
"better" or "worse".
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: J4 (was: Symbols for Logical Operators

_(reply depth: 12)_

- **From:** "Chuck Stevens" <charles.stevens@unisys.com>
- **Date:** 2003-06-09T13:42:30-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bc2rfm$1o5r$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com>`
- **References:** `<bbgn0a$11u7$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <3edc0d2e.367429814@news.optonline.net> <01c329f9$9f7a6520$64ccf943@chottel> <bbiqfd$2j0g$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <bbktdg$lll$1@slb9.atl.mindspring.net> <3ede6c0d.522812173@news.optonline.net> <bbmhd0$fos$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net> <3edf2034.568937758@news.optonline.net> <bbnjem$tnc$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net> <3edfbfac.609768200@news.optonline.net> <bborhv$r06$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net> <3ee21bd9.114483870@news.optonline.net>`

```

"Robert Wagner" <robert@wagner.net> wrote in message
news:3ee21bd9.114483870@news.optonline.net...

> My J4 suggestion provides yet another alternative style, for those who
prefer it
> (me, for one). But the freedom of choice loving locals want to deny me
that
> choice. There appears to be a contradiction here.

No, because as I pointed out elsewhere:  Adding the necessary characters
from ISO/IEC 646 to allow the programmers to use symbols for AND, OR and NOT
via the REPLACE statement provides "yet another alternative style".  Adding
the symbols themselves as being reserved in the contexts in which AND, OR
and NOT might be used in COBOL as abbreviations for those symbols is
"prohibiting the use of these symbols for any other purpose in that
context".

The first is, in my opinion, liberating; the second, however, is ultimately
restrictive.

    -Chuck Stevens
```

…[16 more quoted lines elided]…

Why not allow any text string in REPLACE? This would enable non-English speakers
to express reserved words in their own alphabet (e.g. ISO/IEC 10646, UCS, UTF or
implementor defined).
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: J4 (was: Symbols for Logical Operators

_(reply depth: 14)_

- **From:** "Chuck Stevens" <charles.stevens@unisys.com>
- **Date:** 2003-06-10T09:45:07-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bc51ui$80m$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com>`
- **References:** `<bbgn0a$11u7$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <3edc0d2e.367429814@news.optonline.net> <01c329f9$9f7a6520$64ccf943@chottel> <bbiqfd$2j0g$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <bbktdg$lll$1@slb9.atl.mindspring.net> <3ede6c0d.522812173@news.optonline.net> <bbmhd0$fos$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net> <3edf2034.568937758@news.optonline.net> <bbnjem$tnc$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net> <3edfbfac.609768200@news.optonline.net> <bborhv$r06$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net> <3ee21bd9.114483870@news.optonline.net> <bc2rfm$1o5r$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <3ee59b9a.123233086@news.optonline.net>`

```

"Robert Wagner" <robert@wagner.net> wrote in message
news:3ee59b9a.123233086@news.optonline.net...

> Why not allow any text string in REPLACE? This would enable non-English
speakers
> to express reserved words in their own alphabet (e.g. ISO/IEC 10646, UCS,
UTF or
> implementor defined).

I actually think this is the right direction, but I'm not convinced the
answer is "any text string" for pseudo-text; it introduces too many
variables and too many ambiguities.  Allowing non-English speakers to
express reserved words in their own alphabet is only half the solution, for
the order of components of COBOL statements was developed on the basis of
English grammar.  For a language with a different word order, the effort to
put as much as possible into the native language can easily backfire.  While
this may be a noble effort at *some* point, I think it's a distraction from
the current issue.

Moreover, to assist in portability I believe the components of the
*language* should be expressed in the smallest reasonable set of characters;
I think it needs to be very conservative in this respect.  The "printable
set", plus the space, from ISO/IEC 646 Table 5 strikes me as a reasonable
starting point, and provides a number of new symbols in the process.

Currently, "Pseudo-text-1 shall contain one or more text-words, at least one
of which shall be neither a separator comma nor a separator semicolon."  At
some point I intend to explore extending this rule to allow some specific
thing other than what we now know as text-words (specifically to avoid
changing the definition of that term).

If we added a new category in the COBOL character repertoire -- perhaps
"extended special characters" -- defined as the set !, %, ?, @, [, \, ], ^,
_, `, {, |, } and ~,  which are usable *only* in the formation of a new sort
of word -- perhaps "user-symbol" or some other such otherwise-unused
name --, which in turn are defined only for use in pseudo-text-1 (but not
pseudo-text-2), we'd have the ability to develop "user symbols".  It seems
to me that it would be reasonable for the composition of "user symbols" to
be limited, at least initially, to "basic special characters" and "extended
special characters" (with at least one of the latter being required) to find
out how well everything "shakes down".  Adding "basic digits" and "basic
letters" into this mix risks ambiguity with "user-defined words", which
already can contain "additional characters from the repertoire of ISO/IEC
10646-1" and thus must be approached *VERY* carefully.

> (e.g. ISO/IEC 10646, UCS, UTF or implementor defined).

The last is flat out of the question for portability reasons.  As stated
above, the *smallest* set of characters that can reasonably be considered
portable to *any* platform is more appropriate.    User-defined words can
already contain additional characters from ISO/IEC 10646-1; while I agree
that someday being able to write a COBOL program entirely in hieroglyphics
or cuneiform might be both useful and possible, I think doing so is not
required *today* for *this* particular issue.

    -Chuck Stevens
```

"A snake meets a rabbit by the bank of a stream.

The rabbit looks around to make an escape but the snake smiles and says:
"It's OK. I'm not hungry. Where are you going?"

"I was looking for a way across the stream," the rabbit replies, nervously.

"Well, I'm going across myself and I'll gladly give you a ride if that would
help," says the snake.

"You promise you won't harm me?" says the rabbit.

"I promise." says the snake. "We snakes get some really bad press. We aren't
really that bad. I have a wife and family. Some snakes are really kind and
generous."

The rabbit timidly climbs onto the snake's back and the serpent takes to the
water. As the water rises, the rabbit becomes more and more terrified. But
the snake reassures him, and with strong, sinuous, "s" shaped strokes, makes
it across the stream.

As they climb up the bank the rabbit turns to thank his new friend. As he
does, the snake strikes and has him by the back of the neck.

Bitterly the dying rabbit says: " But you PROMISED you wouldn't harm me..."

"I can't help it," mutters the snake, with genuine regret. "I'm a snake."

Go, Glasshopper, and consider the chances of becoming other than what you
are, for here is the Way to True Enlightenment."

(Takes out ping-pong balls, removes yellow robe - blushes with embarrassment
and puts on pants. Goes back to coding COBOL...)

Pete.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: J4 (was: Symbols for Logical Operators

_(reply depth: 10)_

- **From:** "Chuck Stevens" <charles.stevens@unisys.com>
- **Date:** 2003-06-06T09:04:51-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bbqe3f$2060$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com>`
- **References:** `<bbgn0a$11u7$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <3edc0d2e.367429814@news.optonline.net> <01c329f9$9f7a6520$64ccf943@chottel> <bbiqfd$2j0g$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <bbktdg$lll$1@slb9.atl.mindspring.net> <3ede6c0d.522812173@news.optonline.net> <bbmhd0$fos$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net> <3edf2034.568937758@news.optonline.net> <bbnjem$tnc$1@slb0.atl.mindspring.net> <3edfbfac.609768200@news.optonline.net>`

```

"Robert Wagner" <robert@wagner.net> wrote in message
news:3edfbfac.609768200@news.optonline.net...

> Good idea under normal conditions. Bad idea when there is a political
bias.

Depends.  If nobody else proposes it formally to J4, I'm considering the
suggestion to add backslash ("\") to the "basic special character" list of
the standard.

Presuming that change, the issue of whether a programmer CAN code
    IF A = B /\ (C = D \/ E = F)
would be rendered moot, because a preceding REPLACE would provide for it.

After I wrote my earlier document regarding these two digraphs and
suggesting the possibility of "~" for "NOT", I realized that aside from the
diagraphs there's no other use for "\" in the language, and it would serve
almost as well as a synonym for "NOT".   Thus, by adding a single character
to the list, the programmer is free to use symbols for ALL THREE "logical
operators" through REPLACE.

Then the issue as to whether these symbols should be *standardized* in the
*language* (rather than incorporated in individual programs or through site
convention via REPLACE) would be entirely divorced from the issue as to
whether it's possible to use these abbreviations in conforming programs in
the first place.

I do believe they're two separate issues that should be addressed
separately.

    -Chuck Stevens
```

"Robert Wagner" <robert@wagner.net> wrote in message

Robert, this is totally unfair and unreasonable. (And, besides, "Poor Me" is
a role that doesn't suit you; you are more than capable of  defending your
own position.)

What you have missed is that most of us don't live in your black and white
world. (I mentioned this to you on a previous occasion; you seem to have
great difficulty in recognising shades of grey...)

It isn't about having words OR symbols. There is no reason why we can't have
both. They are not mutually exclusive.
Freedom of choice is a very good thing; having one solution or another
imposed on you is not.

There was no need for you to "switch sides". All you had to do was expand
your horizon.

You were not "STILL wrong"; you were just still missing the fact that there
were more than two options.

Nobody being objective gets shouted down. There may be fierce debate, there
may be strong objection, but once something is posted it cannot be ignored.

(You can fail to respond to it, but, you cannot avoid reading it unless you
ignore the whole thread. I never thought I'd see the day when I would do
that, but I have recently. There are threads here that I simply ignore,
UNLESS there is a new post from someone I consider is "worth reading"...
This is not a situation I enjoy and I didn't think it would happen, but it
has, and you are largely responsible for it. (That's not a criticism; you
have a right to post and I'll defend that right whether I agree with your
posts or not...). Your aggressive dominating approach simply brings out the
worst in people and neither party will let go. This makes for a boring,
pointless, personal debate that is of no interest to anyone else and simply
makes the whole thread unreadable.)

Have you reviewed what happened here? Have you thought about what you might
have done differently, or are you content to conclude that you are right,
and they are all out to get you...?

You can (and hopefully, will) be a valuable contributor to CLC. Provided you
don't destroy it first...<G>

Pete.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: OT - Poor Me - J4 (was: Symbols for Logical Operators

_(reply depth: 10)_

- **From:** "Chuck Stevens" <charles.stevens@unisys.com>
- **Date:** 2003-06-09T14:19:22-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bc2tkq$1pfo$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com>`
- **References:** `<bbgn0a$11u7$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <3edc0d2e.367429814@news.optonline.net> <01c329f9$9f7a6520$64ccf943@chottel> <bbiqfd$2j0g$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <bbktdg$lll$1@slb9.atl.mindspring.net> <3ede6c0d.522812173@news.optonline.net> <bbmhd0$fos$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net> <3edf2034.568937758@news.optonline.net> <3edfd9a1_4@news.athenanews.com> <3ee22e78.119252400@news.optonline.net>`

```

"Robert Wagner" <robert@wagner.net> wrote in message
news:3ee22e78.119252400@news.optonline.net...

> >It isn't about having words OR symbols. There is no reason why we can't
have
> >both. They are not mutually exclusive.
>
> That's ALL my J4 suggestion asks for. If the group encourages choice, why
is
> there opposition?

Because what you are actually doing, in your two-step process -- add the
requisite symbol characters to the table, and then reserve them in this
context -- is basically saying "make them so I can use them the way I want
to, and also make them so that others have *only* the choice to do it my
way, or not at all."   The first gives freedom.  The second takes it away.

> >Freedom of choice is a very good thing; having one solution or another
> >imposed on you is not.

> You have it backwards. I'm asking for choice; the others want to impose
the
> words and/or/not .

No, at least some others want to add some extra symbols to the standard and
let the *programmer* decide how to use them.  You want to add the characters
to the standard (you have to do that to make it part of the syntax in the
first place), and then you want the *standard* to specify that (e.g.) "^" be
an abbreviation for NOT.

When the first step's been done I have no problem with an application
programmer doing it with REPLACE, but if I want to use "^" for something
else, I am not inclined to support your proposal that prevents me from doing
so!  You are not asking for choice, you're asking for "as far as "^" is
concerned, it's my way or not at all."

> What are the options to and/or/not?

For starters, let's try adding "\" to the Basic Special Character table.  I
think that's doable without much violence.  Then you can code
    REPLACE ==/\== by ==AND==, ==\/== by ==OR==, ==\== by ==NOT==.

If the characters ^!|~ exist in ISO/IEC 646 (are they 5E, 21, 7C and 7E
respectively?) then you can code a similar
    REPLACE ==^== by ==AND==, ==|== by ==OR==, ==!== by ==NOT==.
in *your* programs,. and leave me free to code the first of these above,
plus
    REPLACE ==!== by ==OR==, ==~== by NOT== .
for compatibility with ALGOL and standard logical notation, if I so choose,
in *mine*.  Your way says I *can't* use "!" for "OR" as ALGOL does.

Why would you wish to prevent me from doing so, since you've already said
you want to allow everyone to be able to choose whatever floats their boats?

> My postings here aren't remotely close to the material which destroys
> newsgroups.

In your personal experience.  I'm not convinced that's definitive.

    -Chuck Stevens
```

Chuck Stevens wrote:
> For starters, let's try adding "\" to the Basic Special Character table.  I
> think that's doable without much violence.  Then you can code
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> you want to allow everyone to be able to choose whatever floats their boats?

Can't you now say

Replace ==And== by ==Or==, ==Or== by ==And==?

(If you really wanted to be confusing...)  I can see your point, but 
then again, it seems that you could just override any symbol in the 
standard with a replace statement.

I had never seen the pseudo-text format of the replace statement until 
this thread (Alphabets/J4/etc).  I've been playing with it, and it's 
really powerful.  The first line in the Procedure Division of my biggest 
programs is now

Replace ==<> == by ==Not = ==

Why wait for <> to be approved?  I can use it now!  :)

- **From:** "Chuck Stevens" <charles.stevens@unisys.com>
- **Date:** 2003-06-12T13:49:08-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<bcap05$17oo$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com>`
- **References:** `<bbgn0a$11u7$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <3edc0d2e.367429814@news.optonline.net> <01c329f9$9f7a6520$64ccf943@chottel> <bbiqfd$2j0g$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <bbktdg$lll$1@slb9.atl.mindspring.net> <3ede6c0d.522812173@news.optonline.net> <bbmhd0$fos$1@slb6.atl.mindspring.net> <3edf2034.568937758@news.optonline.net> <3edfd9a1_4@news.athenanews.com> <3ee22e78.119252400@news.optonline.net> <bc2tkq$1pfo$1@si05.rsvl.unisys.com> <3EE712EF.5000707@Knology.net>`

```

"LX-i" <DanielJSNOSPAM@Knology.net> wrote in message
news:3EE712EF.5000707@Knology.net...

> Can't you now say
>
> Replace ==And== by ==Or==, ==Or== by ==And==?

Yes, in fact, you can.  My suggestion is to allow, at least in the initial
change to the standard, "new" symbols only before the "by", which would
minimize the risk in this case.

> (If you really wanted to be confusing...)  I can see your point, but
> then again, it seems that you could just override any symbol in the
> standard with a replace statement.

You can today, so long as the symbol's made up of stuff from the COBOL
character set.

> I've been playing with it, and it's
> really powerful.  The first line in the Procedure Division of my biggest
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Yup.

So long as we're talking about "aesthetics" and "symmetry" and the like,
though, "<>" has some problems in that area, largely because "equal" means
two fundamentally different things these days in COBOL.  One of those is a
matter of magnitude comparison; the other relates to equivalence or
matching.  Personally I would rather have distinguished the concept "EQUAL"
from that of "MATCHES" (or, if you will, that of "NOT EQUAL" from that of
"UNEQUAL"), in the manner that Algol's "A = B" is not the same thing as "A
IS B".   While historically "not equal" is indeed a magnitude issue, in some
applications the use of the < and > symbols in combination to mean NOT EQUAL
is misleading.  Not a huge deal, but several have noted it.

I'm also concerned that if we add a formal symbol, say "!" for NOT, we end
up with two symbols for NOT EQUAL.  There was a time when it might have been
possible to add MATCHES and/or IS UNEQUAL TO to the language, and then
having the two symbols "!=" and "<>" might have served a useful purpose.
As it is I think having two different abbreviations adds to confusion more
than clarity.

    -Chuck Stevens
```

```

"Robert Wagner" <robert@wagner.net> wrote in message
news:3ee7c547.39150399@news.optonline.net...
> "Chuck Stevens" <charles.stevens@unisys.com> wrote:
>
> >
>
> Nonsense. Programmers can still REPLACE the symbols with whatever they
want.
>
Robert, I don't WANT to REPLACE the symbols. I don't LIKE REPLACE. (It's bad
enough having to replace pseudotext in COPY books (I avoid them for that
reason and only use them where it really makes sense to...)).

I just want to be able to code WITHOUT HAVING to use the symbols. (Yours, or
anybody else's...).

Is that plain enough?

The ONLY proviso I would put on any amendments to the COBOL language are
that I don't HAVE to use them if I don't want to. (and, of course, that what
has ALWAYS worked, will continue to do so...that is an implicit corollary to
the proviso...)

As long as amendments meet that criterion there will be very few objections.

As long as amendments DON'T meet that criterion, there will strong
objections and long (arguably pointless) debates that will achieve little
apart from waste the time of people who could be better employed doing
something else. (We are already seeing this effect in the departures from
the forum...)

Pete.
